الحجة الرابعة : قالوا : لو كان العالم حادثاً ، لكان الفاعل الأول لم يزل غير فاعل ، وكل ما لم يكن فاعلا فإنه يصير فاعلا على وجه الحكمة ، إلا عند تغير شيء ، لا يكون ذلك التغير من قبله . وذلك في حق الله تعالى محال . فكان يجب أن يمتنع أن يصير فاعلاً بعد أن لم يكن فاعلا ولما كان هذا باطلاً ، علمنا أنه كان فاعلاً لم يزل . فيفتقر ههنا إلى تقرير مقامين : المقام الأول : إن الفاعل الحكيم يمتنع أن يكون فاعلاً بعد أن كان غير فاعل ، إلا عند تغير شيء لا يكون ذلك التغير من قبله . والدليل عليه : إنا إذا فرضنا رجلاً كان جالساً عندنا مدة طويلة بإختياره ثم إنه قام عنا باختياره فهذا التبدل إنما حصل، لأنه حصل تبدل في حالة من الأحوال إلا بإختياره ، مثل إنه قرب وصول الليل ، فقام الرجل عن ذلك المكان ، لذلك السبب . أو تذكر مهما كان قد نسيه ، أو وصل إليه خبر كان غافلاً . فإذا لم يحدث البتة حادث ، ينقل هذا الرجل عن الرأي الأول إلى ضده، امتنع أن يتبدل حاله في الفعل والترك . ونقول : هذا إما أن يكون ممتنعاً ، أو أن لم يمتنع . لكنه يكون سفهاً ، فإن الرجل إذا كان جالساً في داره مدة سبعين سنة ، ولم يتحرك ولم يشتغل بمصلحة ولا بإصلاح حال ، ثم نفر بعد ذلك دفعة واحدة بجد عظيم ، واجتهاد شديد ، وشرع في الأعمال ، وفي نظم المهمات . فإذا قيل له . وما السبب الذي اقتضى الانتقال من الفراغ المتقدم، إلى هذا الاشتغال التام؟ فإذا لم يذكر فيه سبباً البتة، كان ذلك إما ممتنعاً في نفسه، أو كان محض العبث والسفه فيثبت بهذا أن القائل المختار الحكيم لا ينتقل من الترك إلى الفعل إلا بسبب متغير ، ويجب أن يكون ذلك التغير لا من قبله، إذ لو كان من قبله لعاد السؤال الأول فيه . وهو أنه لم غيره في هذا الوقت دون ما قبله وما بعده ؟ وأما إذا كان ذلك التغير ليس من قبله ، صح ذلك . مثل : أنه لما انتهى النهار إلى آخره ، قام الرجل من مكانه ، وذهب إلى الدار ، ولما قرب هجوم الشتاء أقدم الرجل على تحصيل مهمات الشتاء ، فيثبت بما ذكرنا : أن كل ما كان غير فاعل لم يزل ، فإنه يصير فاعلاً إلا لتغير حصل ، لا من قبله . وهذا في حق الفاعل الأول محال . لأن جميع التغيرات إنما حصل بتكوينه وإيجاده، فإمتنع أن يكون تغيره من ترك الفعل إلى تحصيل الفعل ، لأجل تغير وقع لا من جهته ، فلو كان غير فاعل في الأزل ، وجب أن لا يصير فاعلاً في لا يزال وحيث صار فاعلاً ، جارياً مجرى ما إذا قصد الواحد منا ، إلى السفر حال اعتدال الحر والبرد ، فإنه كان الداعي له إلى تحصيل الربح موجوداً قبل ذلك ، إلا أنه كان ينتظر حضور الوقت
The fourth proof: They said: If the world were created, then the first agent would have never ceased to be non-agent, and everything that was not an agent becomes an agent in a wise manner only upon a change of something, that change not being from him. And that regarding God Almighty is impossible. So it would be necessary that it be impossible for Him to become an agent after not having been an agent. And since this is false, we know that He was an agent without ceasing. Thus here we need to establish two stations: The first station: The wise agent is impossible to be an agent after having been non-agent, except upon a change of something that change not being from him. The evidence for it: If we suppose a man who was sitting near us for a long time by his choice, then he stood up from us by his choice, this change only occurred because a change occurred in some state not by his choice, such as the approach of night, so the man stood up from that place for that reason, or he remembered something he had forgotten, or news reached him of which he was unaware. So if no event at all occurs to transfer this man from the first opinion to its opposite, it is impossible for his state to change in action and abandonment. And we say: This is either impossible, or not impossible. But it would be foolishness. For if a man was sitting in his house for seventy years, not moving or engaging in any interest or improvement of his state, then afterwards he jumps up suddenly with great seriousness and intense effort, and begins works and organizing important matters. So if he is asked: What is the reason that necessitated the transition from the previous idleness to this complete occupation? And if he does not mention any reason at all, then that is either impossible in itself, or pure futility and foolishness. Thus it is established by this that the wise voluntary agent does not move from abandonment to action except due to a changing cause, and that change must not be from him, because if it were from him the first question would return concerning it, namely: Why did he change it at this time and not before and after? But if that change is not from him, it is valid. For example: when the day ended, the man stood up from his place and went home, and when winter approached the man proceeded to procure winter necessities. Thus it is established by what we have mentioned that everything that was not an agent without ceasing becomes an agent only due to a change that occurred, not from him. And this is impossible regarding the first agent, because all changes only occur by His creation and bringing into existence. So it is impossible for His change from abandoning action to obtaining action to be due to a change that occurred not from Him. So if He were non-agent in eternity, it would be necessary that He not become an agent in perpetuity. And since He became an agent in perpetuity, we know that He was also an agent in eternity. And let it not be said: The purpose of bringing into existence is to deliver benefit to creatures, because this purpose was desired before, so why did He not begin action before that? And let it not be said: That time was specifically chosen for creation because it was most beneficial for the morally responsible, or because it was determined by the will. For we say: That time which is most beneficial for creating the world over other times, either it occurs by the creation of God Almighty or not by His creation. If it occurs by the creation of God Almighty, the question returns: why did He do it, and not do something else? And if it is not by the creation of God Almighty, then this says that before God Almighty's creation of the world, times existed and changes occurred, so God Almighty's creation of the world at that time becomes analogous to when one of us intends to travel at a time of moderate heat and cold, for the motive for him to obtain profit existed before that, but he was waiting for the arrival of the time.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof (al-hujja al-rabi'a) concerning the eternity of God's action. It begins by stating the opponents' argument: if the world were created (hadith), then the first agent (al-fa'il al-awwal) would have been non-agent (ghayr fa'il) in eternity (lam yazal), and then became an agent, which is impossible for a wise agent (al-fa'il al-hakim) unless a change occurs that is not from him. Since such a change is impossible for God, the world cannot be created; rather, God must be eternally active. The author then says two stations (maqaman) need to be established. The first station argues that a wise agent cannot become active after being inactive except due to an external change. The evidence uses an analogy: a man sitting for a long time who stands up only because of an external factor (like nightfall, remembering something, or news). Without such a factor, the change would be impossible or foolish. If a man sits idle for seventy years and then suddenly works without reason, it is either impossible or pure senselessness. Thus, a wise agent only transitions from inaction to action due to a changing cause (sabab mutaghayyir) that is not from him; otherwise, the question would regress: why did he change at that moment? Then the argument applies to God: all changes are created by Him, so He cannot change due to an external cause. Therefore, if He were inactive in eternity, He would never become active. Since the world exists, He must have been eternally active. The passage then refutes two objections: (1) that the purpose (gharad) of creation is to benefit creatures, which existed before, so why delay? (2) that the time of creation was chosen because it was most beneficial or due to will. The answer to the first: if the time is created by God, the same question returns; if not, then times and changes exist independently, making God's action like a human waiting for a suitable time, which implies temporal precedence.

Key Terms
الحجة الرابعة
الفاعل الأول
لم يزل
حادث
المقام الأول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's inactivity in eternity would be temporary and He could later decide to act.
Correction: The opponents argue that if God were non-agent in eternity, any later action would require an external change, which is impossible for God, so He must be eternally active.

Checkpoint
According to the opponents' argument, why must God be eternally active?
A) Because God cannot become active after inactivity without an external change, which is impossible for Him.
B) Because God desires to create the world.
C) Because time is eternal.
D) Because the world is created.

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof argues that God must be eternally active because any change from inactivity to activity would require an impossible external change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Reflect on your own actions: how often do you act wisely only when circumstances change, rather than from a constant, unchanging intention? How does this contrast with God's eternal agency, and what does it reveal about your dependence on external factors? This lesson challenges you to examine whether your faith in God's constant action shapes your daily trust, or if you live as if God acts only in response to events.
?
If God is eternally active, then His involvement in your life is continuous and not sporadic. Do you truly rely on that constant activity, or do you only turn to Him when you face a change or crisis? What would change in your worship and reliance if you deeply internalized that God never ceases to be your Sustainer and Guide?
?
The argument states that a wise agent only acts upon a change. Consider the areas in your life where you procrastinate or wait for the 'right moment' to act. How does that pattern reflect a reliance on change rather than a steady will? How can you cultivate a more constant, God-aware agency in your own actions, mirroring the eternal agency of God?

The First Station: Wise Agency and External Change
Al-Razi presents the evidence for the first station using the human analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a wise agent cannot transition from inaction to action without an external cause, using the analogy of a man sitting and then standing.

Core Idea
Without a reason, sudden action after long idleness is either impossible or foolish.

In the first station, Al-Razi proves the general principle: a wise agent only becomes active after inactivity due to a change not from himself. He uses a vivid analogy of a man sitting for a long time and then suddenly standing up. Let's examine the evidence and the reasoning that highlights the necessity of an external cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy
Imagine a man sitting by choice for a long time, then standing up. The change in action must be due to an external factor like nightfall or a remembered task. Without any such factor, the change is either impossible or pure foolishness.
Notice the emphasis on 'by choice' – voluntary action is still guided by reasons.
2
Understand the necessary condition
The text argues that a wise agent only moves from abandonment to action upon a changing cause (sabab mutaghayyir) that is not from him. Otherwise, the transition is either impossible (mumtani') or foolish (safah).
This establishes the principle needed for the proof.
3
Apply to the wise agent
If the cause were from the agent, the same question would regress: why did he choose that cause at that time? So the cause must be external.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : قالوا : لو كان العالم حادثاً ، لكان الفاعل الأول لم يزل غير فاعل ، وكل ما لم يكن فاعلا فإنه يصير فاعلا على وجه الحكمة ، إلا عند تغير شيء ، لا يكون ذلك التغير من قبله . وذلك في حق الله تعالى محال . فكان يجب أن يمتنع أن يصير فاعلاً بعد أن لم يكن فاعلا ولما كان هذا باطلاً ، علمنا أنه كان فاعلاً لم يزل . فيفتقر ههنا إلى تقرير مقامين : المقام الأول : إن الفاعل الحكيم يمتنع أن يكون فاعلاً بعد أن كان غير فاعل ، إلا عند تغير شيء لا يكون ذلك التغير من قبله . والدليل عليه : إنا إذا فرضنا رجلاً كان جالساً عندنا مدة طويلة بإختياره ثم إنه قام عنا باختياره فهذا التبدل إنما حصل، لأنه حصل تبدل في حالة من الأحوال إلا بإختياره ، مثل إنه قرب وصول الليل ، فقام الرجل عن ذلك المكان ، لذلك السبب . أو تذكر مهما كان قد نسيه ، أو وصل إليه خبر كان غافلاً . فإذا لم يحدث البتة حادث ، ينقل هذا الرجل عن الرأي الأول إلى ضده، امتنع أن يتبدل حاله في الفعل والترك . ونقول : هذا إما أن يكون ممتنعاً ، أو أن لم يمتنع . لكنه يكون سفهاً ، فإن الرجل إذا كان جالساً في داره مدة سبعين سنة ، ولم يتحرك ولم يشتغل بمصلحة ولا بإصلاح حال ، ثم نفر بعد ذلك دفعة واحدة بجد عظيم ، واجتهاد شديد ، وشرع في الأعمال ، وفي نظم المهمات . فإذا قيل له . وما السبب الذي اقتضى الانتقال من الفراغ المتقدم، إلى هذا الاشتغال التام؟ فإذا لم يذكر فيه سبباً البتة، كان ذلك إما ممتنعاً في نفسه، أو كان محض العبث والسفه فيثبت بهذا أن القائل المختار الحكيم لا ينتقل من الترك إلى الفعل إلا بسبب متغير ، ويجب أن يكون ذلك التغير لا من قبله، إذ لو كان من قبله لعاد السؤال الأول فيه . وهو أنه لم غيره في هذا الوقت دون ما قبله وما بعده ؟ وأما إذا كان ذلك التغير ليس من قبله ، صح ذلك . مثل : أنه لما انتهى النهار إلى آخره ، قام الرجل من مكانه ، وذهب إلى الدار ، ولما قرب هجوم الشتاء أقدم الرجل على تحصيل مهمات الشتاء ، فيثبت بما ذكرنا : أن كل ما كان غير فاعل لم يزل ، فإنه يصير فاعلاً إلا لتغير حصل ، لا من قبله . وهذا في حق الفاعل الأول محال . لأن جميع التغيرات إنما حصل بتكوينه وإيجاده، فإمتنع أن يكون تغيره من ترك الفعل إلى تحصيل الفعل ، لأجل تغير وقع لا من جهته ، فلو كان غير فاعل في الأزل ، وجب أن لا يصير فاعلاً في لا يزال وحيث صار فاعلاً في لا يزال علمنا : أنه كان أيضاً فاعلاً في الأزل ، ولا يقال : الغرض من الإيجاد : إيصال النفع إلى الخلق ، لأن هذا الغرض كان مطلوباً قبل ذلك فلم لم يشرع في الفعل ، قبل ذلك ؟ ولا يقال : ذلك الوقت إنما اختص بالإحداث ، لأنه أصلح للمكلفين ، أو لأنه تعين بسبب الإرادة لأنا نقول : ذلك الوقت الذي هو أصلح لإحداث العالم من سائر الأوقات ، إما أن يحدث بإحداث الله تعالى أو لا بإحداثه فإن حدث بإحداث الله تعالى ، عاد السؤال في أنه : لم فعله ، ولم يفعل غيره ؟ وإن كان لا بإحداث الله تعالى ، فهذا قول بأنه قبل إحداث الله تعالى العالم ، كانت الأوقات موجودة ، والتغيرات حاصلة ، فيصير إحداث الله العالم في ذلك الوقت ، جارياً مجرى ما إذا قصد الواحد منا ، إلى السفر حال اعتدال الحر والبرد ، فإنه كان الداعي له إلى تحصيل الربح موجوداً قبل ذلك ، إلا أنه كان ينتظر حضور الوقت
The fourth proof: They said: If the world were created, then the first agent would have never ceased to be non-agent, and everything that was not an agent becomes an agent in a wise manner only upon a change of something, that change not being from him. And that regarding God Almighty is impossible. So it would be necessary that it be impossible for Him to become an agent after not having been an agent. And since this is false, we know that He was an agent without ceasing. Thus here we need to establish two stations: The first station: The wise agent is impossible to be an agent after having been non-agent, except upon a change of something that change not being from him. The evidence for it: If we suppose a man who was sitting near us for a long time by his choice, then he stood up from us by his choice, this change only occurred because a change occurred in some state not by his choice, such as the approach of night, so the man stood up from that place for that reason, or he remembered something he had forgotten, or news reached him of which he was unaware. So if no event at all occurs to transfer this man from the first opinion to its opposite, it is impossible for his state to change in action and abandonment. And we say: This is either impossible, or not impossible. But it would be foolishness. For if a man was sitting in his house for seventy years, not moving or engaging in any interest or improvement of his state, then afterwards he jumps up suddenly with great seriousness and intense effort, and begins works and organizing important matters. So if he is asked: What is the reason that necessitated the transition from the previous idleness to this complete occupation? And if he does not mention any reason at all, then that is either impossible in itself, or pure futility and foolishness. Thus it is established by this that the wise voluntary agent does not move from abandonment to action except due to a changing cause, and that change must not be from him, because if it were from him the first question would return concerning it, namely: Why did he change it at this time and not before and after? But if that change is not from him, it is valid. For example: when the day ended, the man stood up from his place and went home, and when winter approached the man proceeded to procure winter necessities. Thus it is established by what we have mentioned that everything that was not an agent without ceasing becomes an agent only due to a change that occurred, not from him. And this is impossible regarding the first agent, because all changes only occur by His creation and bringing into existence. So it is impossible for His change from abandoning action to obtaining action to be due to a change that occurred not from Him. So if He were non-agent in eternity, it would be necessary that He not become an agent in perpetuity. And since He became an agent in perpetuity, we know that He was also an agent in eternity. And let it not be said: The purpose of bringing into existence is to deliver benefit to creatures, because this purpose was desired before, so why did He not begin action before that? And let it not be said: That time was specifically chosen for creation because it was most beneficial for the morally responsible, or because it was determined by the will. For we say: That time which is most beneficial for creating the world over other times, either it occurs by the creation of God Almighty or not by His creation. If it occurs by the creation of God Almighty, the question returns: why did He do it, and not do something else? And if it is not by the creation of God Almighty, then this says that before God Almighty's creation of the world, times existed and changes occurred, so God Almighty's creation of the world at that time becomes analogous to when one of us intends to travel at a time of moderate heat and cold, for the motive for him to obtain profit existed before that, but he was waiting for the arrival of the time.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof (al-hujja al-rabi'a) concerning the eternity of God's action. It begins by stating the opponents' argument: if the world were created (hadith), then the first agent (al-fa'il al-awwal) would have been non-agent (ghayr fa'il) in eternity (lam yazal), and then became an agent, which is impossible for a wise agent (al-fa'il al-hakim) unless a change occurs that is not from him. Since such a change is impossible for God, the world cannot be created; rather, God must be eternally active. The author then says two stations (maqaman) need to be established. The first station argues that a wise agent cannot become active after being inactive except due to an external change. The evidence uses an analogy: a man sitting for a long time who stands up only because of an external factor (like nightfall, remembering something, or news). Without such a factor, the change would be impossible or foolish. If a man sits idle for seventy years and then suddenly works without reason, it is either impossible or pure senselessness. Thus, a wise agent only transitions from inaction to action due to a changing cause (sabab mutaghayyir) that is not from him; otherwise, the question would regress: why did he change at that moment? Then the argument applies to God: all changes are created by Him, so He cannot change due to an external cause. Therefore, if He were inactive in eternity, He would never become active. Since the world exists, He must have been eternally active. The passage then refutes two objections: (1) that the purpose (gharad) of creation is to benefit creatures, which existed before, so why delay? (2) that the time of creation was chosen because it was most beneficial or due to will. The answer to the first: if the time is created by God, the same question returns; if not, then times and changes exist independently, making God's action like a human waiting for a suitable time, which implies temporal precedence.

Key Terms
المقام الأول
الفاعل الحكيم
سفهاً
عبث
سبب متغير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that a wise agent can arbitrarily change without any reason.
Correction: The analogy shows that even voluntary changes require a reason (external cause) to be rational; otherwise, the action is either impossible or foolish.

Checkpoint
According to the first station, why can a wise agent not become active after inactivity without an external change?
A) Because the agent would need a new desire, which is impossible.
B) Because without an external change, the transition would be either impossible or pure foolishness.
C) Because the agent must always be active.
D) Because time is eternal.

Key Takeaway
A wise agent's transition from inaction to action always requires an external cause; otherwise, the change is irrational.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time you made a sudden change in your life—a decision to start something new or abandon a long-standing habit. What was the external cause? If you cannot name one, does that make your action foolish? How does this lesson challenge you to examine your motives before God?
?
Al-Razi argues that even a wise human agent cannot change without an external reason. How does this affect your understanding of God's actions? Are you willing to trust that every divine command or trial has a wise cause, even when you do not see it? What would it mean for your faith if you believed God acts without reason?
?
The passage says a man who sits idly for seventy years then suddenly acts without cause is acting foolishly. Where in your spiritual life have you been 'sitting'—neglecting prayer, charity, or repentance—expecting that a sudden change could happen without a real reason? What external cause must you seek (like the reminder of death or the arrival of Ramadan) to move you to action?

Causality and Created Things
beginner
4 min
Applying the Principle to God
Al-Razi applies the first station's principle to God to prove His eternal activity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the principle of wise agency leads to the conclusion that God must be eternally active.

Core Idea
If God were non-agent in eternity, He would need an external change—impossible for Him.

Now that the principle is established—that any agent moving from inaction to action requires an external change—we apply it to God. Since all changes are created by God, an external change is impossible. Therefore, if God were inactive in eternity, He would never become active. Since we see activity (the world), He must have always been active.

Guided Path
1
Recall the principle
From the first station: anything that was non-agent becomes agent only due to a change not from itself.
This is the key premise.
2
Apply to God
All changes are created by God (by His takwin and ijad). So no change can occur that is not from Him. Therefore, God cannot have an external change to trigger activity.
3
Draw the conclusion
If God were non-agent in eternity, He would never become agent. But the world exists, so He must have always been agent.
This refutes the opponents' original claim.

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof (al-hujja al-rabi'a) concerning the eternity of God's action. It begins by stating the opponents' argument: if the world were created (hadith), then the first agent (al-fa'il al-awwal) would have been non-agent (ghayr fa'il) in eternity (lam yazal), and then became an agent, which is impossible for a wise agent (al-fa'il al-hakim) unless a change occurs that is not from him. Since such a change is impossible for God, the world cannot be created; rather, God must be eternally active. The author then says two stations (maqaman) need to be established. The first station argues that a wise agent cannot become active after being inactive except due to an external change. The evidence uses an analogy: a man sitting for a long time who stands up only because of an external factor (like nightfall, remembering something, or news). Without such a factor, the change would be impossible or foolish. If a man sits idle for seventy years and then suddenly works without reason, it is either impossible or pure senselessness. Thus, a wise agent only transitions from inaction to action due to a changing cause (sabab mutaghayyir) that is not from him; otherwise, the question would regress: why did he change at that moment? Then the argument applies to God: all changes are created by Him, so He cannot change due to an external cause. Therefore, if He were inactive in eternity, He would never become active. Since the world exists, He must have been eternally active. The passage then refutes two objections: (1) that the purpose (gharad) of creation is to benefit creatures, which existed before, so why delay? (2) that the time of creation was chosen because it was most beneficial or due to will. The answer to the first: if the time is created by God, the same question returns; if not, then times and changes exist independently, making God's action like a human waiting for a suitable time, which implies temporal precedence.

Misconception: Some think God could have been inactive and then decided to act without any change.

Why can God not transition from non-agent to agent according to this passage?
A) Because God is inherently active.
B) Because all changes are created by God, so an external change is impossible.
C) Because time does not exist.
D) Because God has no free will.

Key Takeaway
God's eternal activity is proven because He cannot have an external change to initiate action; therefore, He must have always been active.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is eternally active and never passive, what does that require of your attitude toward His involvement in every detail of your life, including moments when you feel neglected by Him?
?
The argument shows that God cannot become an agent because He is the source of all change. How does this truth confront any thought you have entertained that God is distant or waiting to act only after you initiate something?
?
Since God's agency is eternal and without beginning, how should this reshape your reliance on Him in this very moment—knowing that He never had a moment of inaction and never will?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
5 min
Refuting Objections to the Proof
Al-Razi refutes two objections regarding the purpose and timing of creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi refutes two objections: that God's purpose is to benefit creation, and that the time of creation was chosen for optimal benefit.

Core Idea
Both objections fail because they either regress or imply temporal precedence.

After establishing the proof, Al-Razi addresses two potential objections. The first says God created to benefit creatures, which existed before creation. The second says the time of creation was chosen because it was most beneficial or by will. Al-Razi shows that both lead to either an infinite regress or the assumption of pre-existing times, which undermines the opponents' position.

Guided Path
1
Read the first objection and response
Objection: The purpose (gharad) of creation is to benefit creatures, a purpose that existed before. Why didn't God act earlier? The response: This question remains unanswered.
The objection assumes that the purpose existed prior to creation.
2
Read the second objection and response
Objection: The time was chosen because it was most beneficial or due to will. Response: If that time is created by God, the same question returns; if not, then times and changes exist independently, implying God waited like a human.
This weakens the opponents' claim.
3
Understand the implication
Both objections fail to provide a reason that doesn't lead to a regress or acknowledge external factors.

الحجة الرابعة : قالوا : لو كان العالم حادثاً ، لكان الفاعل الأول لم يزل غير فاعل ، وكل ما لم يكن فاعلا فإنه يصير فاعلا على وجه الحكمة ، إلا عند تغير شيء ، لا يكون ذلك التغير من قبله . وذلك في حق الله تعالى محال . فكان يجب أن يمتنع أن يصير فاعلاً بعد أن لم يكن فاعلا ولما كان هذا باطلاً ، علمنا أنه كان فاعلاً لم يزل . فيفتقر ههنا إلى تقرير مقامين : المقام الأول : إن الفاعل الحكيم يمتنع أن يكون فاعلاً بعد أن كان غير فاعل ، إلا عند تغير شيء لا يكون ذلك التغير من قبله . والدليل عليه : إنا إذا فرضنا رجلاً كان جالساً عندنا مدة طويلة بإختياره ثم إنه قام عنا باختياره فهذا التبدل إنما حصل، لأنه حصل تبدل في حالة من الأحوال إلا بإختياره ، مثل إنه قرب وصول الليل ، فقام الرجل عن ذلك المكان ، لذلك السبب . أو تذكر مهما كان قد نسيه ، أو وصل إليه خبر كان غافلاً . فإذا لم يحدث البتة حادث ، ينقل هذا الرجل عن الرأي الأول إلى ضده، امتنع أن يتبدل حاله في الفعل والترك . ونقول : هذا إما أن يكون ممتنعاً ، أو أن لم يمتنع . لكنه يكون سفهاً ، فإن الرجل إذا كان جالساً في داره مدة سبعين سنة ، ولم يتحرك ولم يشتغل بمصلحة ولا بإصلاح حال ، ثم نفر بعد ذلك دفعة واحدة بجد عظيم ، واجتهاد شديد ، وشرع في الأعمال ، وفي نظم المهمات . فإذا قيل له . وما السبب الذي اقتضى الانتقال من الفراغ المتقدم، إلى هذا الاشتغال التام؟ فإذا لم يذكر فيه سبباً البتة، كان ذلك إما ممتنعاً في نفسه، أو كان محض العبث والسفه فيثبت بهذا أن القائل المختار الحكيم لا ينتقل من الترك إلى الفعل إلا بسبب متغير ، ويجب أن يكون ذلك التغير لا من قبله، إذ لو كان من قبله لعاد السؤال الأول فيه . وهو أنه لم غيره في هذا الوقت دون ما قبله وما بعده ؟ وأما إذا كان ذلك التغير ليس من قبله ، صح ذلك . مثل : أنه لما انتهى النهار إلى آخره ، قام الرجل من مكانه ، وذهب إلى الدار ، ولما قرب هجوم الشتاء أقدم الرجل على تحصيل مهمات الشتاء ، فيثبت بما ذكرنا : أن كل ما كان غير فاعل لم يزل ، فإنه يصير فاعلاً إلا لتغير حصل ، لا من قبله . وهذا في حق الفاعل الأول محال . لأن جميع التغيرات إنما حصل بتكوينه وإيجاده، فإمتنع أن يكون تغيره من ترك الفعل إلى تحصيل الفعل ، لأجل تغير وقع لا من جهته ، فلو كان غير فاعل في الأزل ، وجب أن لا يصير فاعلاً في لا يزال وحيث صار فاعلاً في لا يزال علمنا : أنه كان أيضاً فاعلاً في الأزل ، ولا يقال : الغرض من الإيجاد : إيصال النفع إلى الخلق ، لأن هذا الغرض كان مطلوباً قبل ذلك فلم لم يشرع في الفعل ، قبل ذلك ؟ ولا يقال : ذلك الوقت إنما اختص بالإحداث ، لأنه أصلح للمكلفين ، أو لأنه تعين بسبب الإرادة لأنا نقول : ذلك الوقت الذي هو أصلح لإحداث العالم من سائر الأوقات ، إما أن يحدث بإحداث الله تعالى أو لا بإحداثه فإن حدث بإحداث الله تعالى ، عاد السؤال في أنه : لم فعله ، ولم يفعل غيره ؟ وإن كان لا بإحداث الله تعالى ، فهذا قول بأنه قبل إحداث الله تعالى العالم ، كانت الأوقات موجودة ، والتغيرات حاصلة ، فيصير إحداث الله العالم في ذلك الوقت ، جارياً مجرى ما إذا قصد الواحد منا ، إلى السفر حال اعتدال الحر والبرد ، فإنه كان الداعي له إلى تحصيل الربح موجوداً قبل ذلك ، إلا أنه كان ينتظر حضور الوقت
The fourth proof: They said: If the world were created, then the first agent would have never ceased to be non-agent, and everything that was not an agent becomes an agent in a wise manner only upon a change of something, that change not being from him. And that regarding God Almighty is impossible. So it would be necessary that it be impossible for Him to become an agent after not having been an agent. And since this is false, we know that He was an agent without ceasing. Thus here we need to establish two stations: The first station: The wise agent is impossible to be an agent after having been non-agent, except upon a change of something that change not being from him. The evidence for it: If we suppose a man who was sitting near us for a long time by his choice, then he stood up from us by his choice, this change only occurred because a change occurred in some state not by his choice, such as the approach of night, so the man stood up from that place for that reason, or he remembered something he had forgotten, or news reached him of which he was unaware. So if no event at all occurs to transfer this man from the first opinion to its opposite, it is impossible for his state to change in action and abandonment. And we say: This is either impossible, or not impossible. But it would be foolishness. For if a man was sitting in his house for seventy years, not moving or engaging in any interest or improvement of his state, then afterwards he jumps up suddenly with great seriousness and intense effort, and begins works and organizing important matters. So if he is asked: What is the reason that necessitated the transition from the previous idleness to this complete occupation? And if he does not mention any reason at all, then that is either impossible in itself, or pure futility and foolishness. Thus it is established by this that the wise voluntary agent does not move from abandonment to action except due to a changing cause, and that change must not be from him, because if it were from him the first question would return concerning it, namely: Why did he change it at this time and not before and after? But if that change is not from him, it is valid. For example: when the day ended, the man stood up from his place and went home, and when winter approached the man proceeded to procure winter necessities. Thus it is established by what we have mentioned that everything that was not an agent without ceasing becomes an agent only due to a change that occurred, not from him. And this is impossible regarding the first agent, because all changes only occur by His creation and bringing into existence. So it is impossible for His change from abandoning action to obtaining action to be due to a change that occurred not from Him. So if He were non-agent in eternity, it would be necessary that He not become an agent in perpetuity. And since He became an agent in perpetuity, we know that He was also an agent in eternity. And let it not be said: The purpose of bringing into existence is to deliver benefit to creatures, because this purpose was desired before, so why did He not begin action before that? And let it not be said: That time was specifically chosen for creation because it was most beneficial for the morally responsible, or because it was determined by the will. For we say: That time which is most beneficial for creating the world over other times, either it occurs by the creation of God Almighty or not by His creation. If it occurs by the creation of God Almighty, the question returns: why did He do it, and not do something else? And if it is not by the creation of God Almighty, then this says that before God Almighty's creation of the world, times existed and changes occurred, so God Almighty's creation of the world at that time becomes analogous to when one of us intends to travel at a time of moderate heat and cold, for the motive for him to obtain profit existed before that, but he was waiting for the arrival of the time.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof (al-hujja al-rabi'a) concerning the eternity of God's action. It begins by stating the opponents' argument: if the world were created (hadith), then the first agent (al-fa'il al-awwal) would have been non-agent (ghayr fa'il) in eternity (lam yazal), and then became an agent, which is impossible for a wise agent (al-fa'il al-hakim) unless a change occurs that is not from him. Since such a change is impossible for God, the world cannot be created; rather, God must be eternally active. The author then says two stations (maqaman) need to be established. The first station argues that a wise agent cannot become active after being inactive except due to an external change. The evidence uses an analogy: a man sitting for a long time who stands up only because of an external factor (like nightfall, remembering something, or news). Without such a factor, the change would be impossible or foolish. If a man sits idle for seventy years and then suddenly works without reason, it is either impossible or pure senselessness. Thus, a wise agent only transitions from inaction to action due to a changing cause (sabab mutaghayyir) that is not from him; otherwise, the question would regress: why did he change at that moment? Then the argument applies to God: all changes are created by Him, so He cannot change due to an external cause. Therefore, if He were inactive in eternity, He would never become active. Since the world exists, He must have been eternally active. The passage then refutes two objections: (1) that the purpose (gharad) of creation is to benefit creatures, which existed before, so why delay? (2) that the time of creation was chosen because it was most beneficial or due to will. The answer to the first: if the time is created by God, the same question returns; if not, then times and changes exist independently, making God's action like a human waiting for a suitable time, which implies temporal precedence.

Key Terms
غرض
إصلاح
مصلحة
إرادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's purpose (gharad) explains why He created at a specific time.
Correction: The argument shows that if purpose existed before, then the question 'why then?' remains. Purpose alone does not explain the timing.

Checkpoint
What does Al-Razi say about the objection that the time of creation was chosen because it was most beneficial?
A) He accepts it as a valid explanation.
B) He argues that if that time is created by God, the same question returns; if not, times pre-exist, making God like a human waiting.
C) He says it is impossible for a time to be most beneficial.
D) He says the objection is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
The objections based on purpose and optimal timing fail because they either lead to regress or imply independent time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself questioning why God created the world when He did, or why He does things at certain times? This lesson shows that such questions, if not grounded, lead to infinite regress. How does this realization confront your own tendency to demand explanations for God's timing?
?
The objection assumes that God's purpose must be for the benefit of creatures, which seems reasonable. But Al-Razi shows that this assumption doesn't solve the timing problem. Do you sometimes assume that God's actions must fit within your framework of what is beneficial or just? How does this lesson challenge you to submit to His wisdom without requiring it to align with your own expectations?
?
Imagine yourself before God, realizing that you had questioned His timing. Would you be satisfied with the answer that He simply willed it? This lesson pushes you to accept that God's will is the ultimate reason, not needing external justification. What is stopping you from surrendering to that truth today?

The Necessity of an Act When All Preponderators Are Present
Proof that an act is necessary when all preponderators are present.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the presence of all preponderators (complete power, decisive will, etc.) logically necessitates the act, and why this conclusion is established through a proof by contradiction and avoidance of infinite regress.

Core Idea
When all preponderators are present, the act becomes necessary — the foundation of rational theology.

In this passage, the author argues that for any possible act, once all conditions and preponderators are fully present, the act must necessarily occur. This is not physical compulsion but rational necessity. The proof examines what would happen if omission were still possible, leading to either an infinite regress or an effect without a cause — both impossible. Understanding this principle is crucial for later discussions on divine action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial claim
Read the first sentence: a preponderator (murajjih) is necessary for preference. This sets up the argument.
The second division refers to the necessity of a preponderator.
2
Examine the scenario with all preponderators
The author lists the preponderators: complete power, decisive will, time, instrument, benefit, and absence of obstacles. Then he considers whether omission (tark) is possible.
3
Follow the logical branches
If omission is possible, then the specification of time for act vs. omission either depends on another preponderator or not. Both lead to contradictions: the first makes the original preponderator incomplete, the second allows a possible to occur without a preponderator (impossible). Also, if after adding a preponderator the act is not necessary, infinite regress follows.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
4
Reach the conclusion
Since all alternatives are impossible, it is established that the act is necessary (wajib) when all preponderators are present, and impossible when any condition is missing.
This conclusion applies to all agents, including God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني : وهو أنه لا بد في حصول هذا الرجحان من مرجح . فنقول : إذا حصلت المرجحات بأسرها. وهي القدرة التامة ، والإرادة الجازمة الخالية عن الفتور وحصل الوقت والآلة والمصلحة ، وزالت الموانع بأسرها، فمع حصول هذه المرجحات ، إما أن يكون الترك ممكناً ، أو غير ممكن . فإن كان ممكناً فمع حصول هذه المرجحات ، لا يمتنع أن يحصل الفعل تارة ، والترك أخرى ، فاختصاص أحد الوقتين بالفعل ، والوقت الآخر بالترك ، إما أن يتوقف على مرجح ، أو لا يتوقف. فإن كان الأول لم يكن الحاصل قبل انضمام هذا المرجح إليه مرجحاً تاماً . لكنا فرضناه كذلك . هذا خلف . وأيضاً : فعند انضمام هذا المرجح إليه إما أن يكون حصول الفعل واجباً ، أو لا يكون . فإن لم يكن واجباً عاد التقسيم الأول فيه ، وافتقر إلى مرجح آخر ، ولزم التسلسل ، وهو محال . وإن لم يتوقف على مرجح فقد حصل الممكن المتساوي لا لمرجح ، وهو محال . ولما بطلت هذه الأقسام ، ثبت : أن الفعل واجب الحصول عند حصول كل المرجحات ، وممتنع الحصول عند اختلال قيد من القيود المعتبرة في حصول ذلك الرجحان . وإذا ثبت هذا ، فنقول : القادر له حالتان : أحدهما : أن يكون كل ما لا بد منه في المؤثرية حاصلاً في الأزل والأخرى : أن لا يكون هذا المجموع حاصلا أما الحالة الأولى : فإنه يجب صدور الفعل عنه ، ويمتنع أن لا يصدر وأما الحالة الثانية : فإنه يمتنع صدور الفعل عنه ، ويجب عدمه . وعلى هذا التقدير فإنه لا يبقى فرق بين القادر وبين الموجب. بل الفرق : أن شرائط التأثير في حق القادر سريعة التغير ، فإذا حصلت بعد أن كانت معدومة ، صار القادر واجب التأثير . وإذا زالت بعد أن كانت موجودة ، صار ممتنع التأثير ، إلا أن هذا التغير إنما يعقل في حق من تكون مؤثريته موقوفة على شرائط منفصلة عن ذاته، أما الحق سبحانه فإن تأثيره فيما سواه غير موقوف على شرائط منفصلة ذاته ، لأنه تعالى مبدأ لكل ما سواه، فيمتنع أن يكون تأثيره فيما سواه موقوفاً على شرط منفصل، بل يجب أن يكون تأثيره في غيره لمحض ذاته ، ولوازم ذاته . ولما كانت ذاته ولوازم ذاته : ممتنعة التغير . كان تأثيره في غيره أيضاً : ممتنع التغير . فهذا هو الكلام القوي في هذا الباب
As for the second division: It is that a preponderator is necessary for the occurrence of this preference. We say: When all the preponderators are obtained, which are complete power (qudra tamma) and decisive will (irada jazima) free from languor, and the time, instrument, and benefit are obtained, and all obstacles are removed, then with the presence of these preponderators, either omission (tark) is possible or not possible. If it is possible, then with the presence of these preponderators, it is not impossible that the act occurs sometimes and omission at other times. So the specification of one time for the act and another time for omission either depends on a preponderator or does not depend. If the first, then what was obtained before the attachment of this preponderator to it was not a complete preponderator, but we assumed it to be so — this is a contradiction. Also, when this preponderator is attached to it, either the occurrence of the act is necessary or not. If it is not necessary, the first division returns to it, and it requires another preponderator, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul), which is impossible. And if it does not depend on a preponderator, then the equally balanced possible would have occurred without a preponderator, which is impossible. Since these divisions are invalid, it is established that the act is necessary upon the presence of all the preponderators, and impossible upon the disruption of any of the conditions considered for that preference. And when this is established, we say: The capable agent (qadir) has two states: one is that everything necessary for effectiveness is present in eternity, and the other is that this totality is not present. As for the first state, the act must issue from him, and it is impossible that it does not issue. As for the second state, it is impossible for the act to issue from him, and its non-existence is necessary. On this basis, there remains no difference between the capable agent (qadir) and the necessitating cause (mujib). Rather, the difference is that the conditions of effecting in the case of the capable agent are quickly changing; so when they are obtained after having been absent, the capable agent becomes necessarily effective. And when they cease after having been present, he becomes impossible of effecting. However, this change is only conceivable for one whose effectiveness depends on conditions separate from his essence. As for the Truth, Exalted is He, His effecting of other than Him is not dependent on conditions separate from His essence, because He, Exalted, is the origin (mabda') of everything other than Him. Therefore, it is impossible that His effecting of other than Him be dependent on a separate condition. Rather, His effecting of other than Him must be solely by His essence and the necessities of His essence. And since His essence and the necessities of His essence are impossible of change, His effecting of other than Him is also impossible of change. This is the strong discussion in this subject.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a detailed argument establishing the necessity of a preponderator (murajjih) for the occurrence of a possible act. It defines the second division: that a preponderator is necessary. It then examines the scenario when all preponderators are present (complete power, decisive will, time, instrument, benefit, and absence of obstacles). It argues that if omission were still possible with all preponderators present, then the specification of a particular time for the act would require another preponderator, leading to infinite regress or to preference without a preponderator, both impossible. Therefore, when all preponderators are present, the act is necessary (wajib) and when any condition is missing, it is impossible. It then applies this to the capable agent (qadir), showing that in the state where all conditions are present in eternity, the act necessarily issues; in the state where they are not, it necessarily does not. This eliminates the difference between the capable agent and the necessitating cause (mujib) except that the conditions for the capable agent are changeable. However, for God (al-Haqq), whose essence is unchanging and who is the origin of everything, His effecting is not dependent on separate conditions; thus His effecting is also unchanging — that is, necessary.

Key Terms
مرجح
قدرة تامة
إرادة جازمة
مانع
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the capable agent can freely choose to act or not even when all preponderators are present.
Correction: The passage proves that when all preponderators (complete power, decisive will, etc.) are present, the act is necessary and cannot be omitted. This is a rational necessity, not a physical compulsion.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the act when all preponderators (complete power, decisive will, absence of obstacles, etc.) are present?
A) The act is possible but not necessary.
B) The act is necessary and its omission is impossible.
C) The act is impossible.
D) The agent remains free to act or not.

Key Takeaway
When all preponderators are present, the act becomes rationally necessary — this principle underlies all discussions of causation and divine action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you have the complete power, decisive will, time, and tools to fulfill an obligation (like prayer or charity), yet you omit it, which preponderator is actually missing? Is your will truly 'decisive and free from languor'? Examine your heart.
?
Consider a sin you repeatedly commit. What obstacle remains that you refuse to remove? Are you relying on God's mercy while neglecting the removal of that obstacle? What would it take for you to make all preponderators present for obedience?
?
You claim to believe that God's act is necessary when His complete power and will align—yet do you live as if your own acts are determined by the preponderators within your control? What is the one preponderator you have been neglecting that would make your obedience inevitable?

Causality and Created Things

Divine Action: Unchanging Necessity vs. Changing Conditions
Application of the principle to God: His action is eternally necessary due to His unchanging essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why for God there is no difference between the capable agent and the necessitating cause, and how God's action is eternal and unchanging due to His essence.

Core Idea
For God, the act is eternally necessary because His essence and necessities are unchanging.

Having established that an act is necessary when all conditions are present, the author now applies this to the concept of a capable agent (qadir). He shows that if the conditions are present eternally, the act is eternal and necessary. This seems to collapse the distinction between the capable agent and the necessitating cause (mujib). However, the difference lies in the changeability of conditions for created agents. For God, whose essence is the source of all things, there are no separate conditions; His action is an eternal necessity of His essence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two states of the capable agent
The author says the qadir has two states: either all conditions for effectiveness are present in eternity (azal) or they are not. In the first, the act necessarily issues; in the second, it necessarily does not.
This eliminates the difference between qadir and mujib in terms of necessity.
2
Recognize the proposed difference
The difference is that for created agents, the conditions (shara'it) are separate from the essence and quickly change. When they are present, the agent becomes necessarily effective; when they vanish, he becomes impossible of effecting.
3
Apply to God
For God, there are no conditions separate from His essence because He is the origin of everything. His effecting is solely by His essence and the necessities (lawazim) of His essence.
His essence is unchanging, so His effecting is also unchanging.
4
Conclude the argument
Since God's essence and its necessities are immutable, His effecting is also immutable — that is, necessary and eternal. This resolves the apparent problem of distinguishing qadir from mujib.
This is the 'strong discussion' in this topic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني : وهو أنه لا بد في حصول هذا الرجحان من مرجح . فنقول : إذا حصلت المرجحات بأسرها. وهي القدرة التامة ، والإرادة الجازمة الخالية عن الفتور وحصل الوقت والآلة والمصلحة ، وزالت الموانع بأسرها، فمع حصول هذه المرجحات ، إما أن يكون الترك ممكناً ، أو غير ممكن . فإن كان ممكناً فمع حصول هذه المرجحات ، لا يمتنع أن يحصل الفعل تارة ، والترك أخرى ، فاختصاص أحد الوقتين بالفعل ، والوقت الآخر بالترك ، إما أن يتوقف على مرجح ، أو لا يتوقف. فإن كان الأول لم يكن الحاصل قبل انضمام هذا المرجح إليه مرجحاً تاماً . لكنا فرضناه كذلك . هذا خلف . وأيضاً : فعند انضمام هذا المرجح إليه إما أن يكون حصول الفعل واجباً ، أو لا يكون . فإن لم يكن واجباً عاد التقسيم الأول فيه ، وافتقر إلى مرجح آخر ، ولزم التسلسل ، وهو محال . وإن لم يتوقف على مرجح فقد حصل الممكن المتساوي لا لمرجح ، وهو محال . ولما بطلت هذه الأقسام ، ثبت : أن الفعل واجب الحصول عند حصول كل المرجحات ، وممتنع الحصول عند اختلال قيد من القيود المعتبرة في حصول ذلك الرجحان . وإذا ثبت هذا ، فنقول : القادر له حالتان : أحدهما : أن يكون كل ما لا بد منه في المؤثرية حاصلاً في الأزل والأخرى : أن لا يكون هذا المجموع حاصلا أما الحالة الأولى : فإنه يجب صدور الفعل عنه ، ويمتنع أن لا يصدر وأما الحالة الثانية : فإنه يمتنع صدور الفعل عنه ، ويجب عدمه . وعلى هذا التقدير فإنه لا يبقى فرق بين القادر وبين الموجب. بل الفرق : أن شرائط التأثير في حق القادر سريعة التغير ، فإذا حصلت بعد أن كانت معدومة ، صار القادر واجب التأثير . وإذا زالت بعد أن كانت موجودة ، صار ممتنع التأثير ، إلا أن هذا التغير إنما يعقل في حق من تكون مؤثريته موقوفة على شرائط منفصلة عن ذاته، أما الحق سبحانه فإن تأثيره فيما سواه غير موقوف على شرائط منفصلة ذاته ، لأنه تعالى مبدأ لكل ما سواه، فيمتنع أن يكون تأثيره فيما سواه موقوفاً على شرط منفصل، بل يجب أن يكون تأثيره في غيره لمحض ذاته ، ولوازم ذاته . ولما كانت ذاته ولوازم ذاته : ممتنعة التغير . كان تأثيره في غيره أيضاً : ممتنع التغير . فهذا هو الكلام القوي في هذا الباب
As for the second division: It is that a preponderator is necessary for the occurrence of this preference. We say: When all the preponderators are obtained, which are complete power (qudra tamma) and decisive will (irada jazima) free from languor, and the time, instrument, and benefit are obtained, and all obstacles are removed, then with the presence of these preponderators, either omission (tark) is possible or not possible. If it is possible, then with the presence of these preponderators, it is not impossible that the act occurs sometimes and omission at other times. So the specification of one time for the act and another time for omission either depends on a preponderator or does not depend. If the first, then what was obtained before the attachment of this preponderator to it was not a complete preponderator, but we assumed it to be so — this is a contradiction. Also, when this preponderator is attached to it, either the occurrence of the act is necessary or not. If it is not necessary, the first division returns to it, and it requires another preponderator, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul), which is impossible. And if it does not depend on a preponderator, then the equally balanced possible would have occurred without a preponderator, which is impossible. Since these divisions are invalid, it is established that the act is necessary upon the presence of all the preponderators, and impossible upon the disruption of any of the conditions considered for that preference. And when this is established, we say: The capable agent (qadir) has two states: one is that everything necessary for effectiveness is present in eternity, and the other is that this totality is not present. As for the first state, the act must issue from him, and it is impossible that it does not issue. As for the second state, it is impossible for the act to issue from him, and its non-existence is necessary. On this basis, there remains no difference between the capable agent (qadir) and the necessitating cause (mujib). Rather, the difference is that the conditions of effecting in the case of the capable agent are quickly changing; so when they are obtained after having been absent, the capable agent becomes necessarily effective. And when they cease after having been present, he becomes impossible of effecting. However, this change is only conceivable for one whose effectiveness depends on conditions separate from his essence. As for the Truth, Exalted is He, His effecting of other than Him is not dependent on conditions separate from His essence, because He, Exalted, is the origin (mabda') of everything other than Him. Therefore, it is impossible that His effecting of other than Him be dependent on a separate condition. Rather, His effecting of other than Him must be solely by His essence and the necessities of His essence. And since His essence and the necessities of His essence are impossible of change, His effecting of other than Him is also impossible of change. This is the strong discussion in this subject.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a detailed argument establishing the necessity of a preponderator (murajjih) for the occurrence of a possible act. It defines the second division: that a preponderator is necessary. It then examines the scenario when all preponderators are present (complete power, decisive will, time, instrument, benefit, and absence of obstacles). It argues that if omission were still possible with all preponderators present, then the specification of a particular time for the act would require another preponderator, leading to infinite regress or to preference without a preponderator, both impossible. Therefore, when all preponderators are present, the act is necessary (wajib) and when any condition is missing, it is impossible. It then applies this to the capable agent (qadir), showing that in the state where all conditions are present in eternity, the act necessarily issues; in the state where they are not, it necessarily does not. This eliminates the difference between the capable agent and the necessitating cause (mujib) except that the conditions for the capable agent are changeable. However, for God (al-Haqq), whose essence is unchanging and who is the origin of everything, His effecting is not dependent on separate conditions; thus His effecting is also unchanging — that is, necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's ability to act is like a human's ability, with free choice and changing conditions.
Correction: God's essence is unchanging and not dependent on separate conditions; therefore His action is eternally necessary and unchanging, which does not detract from His perfection.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is God's effecting of other than Him unchanging?
A) Because He has complete power.
B) Because His essence and its necessities are impossible of change.
C) Because He has no will.
D) Because conditions for Him are quickly changing.

Key Takeaway
For God, the act is an eternal necessary consequence of His unchanging essence, not dependent on any external conditions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given that God's action is eternally necessary from His unchanging essence, do you truly believe that nothing in your life happens by chance or human power alone? How does that reshape your trust in Him when you face uncertainty? Will you consciously attribute every outcome to His necessary will today?
?
If God's effecting is not dependent on any conditions separate from His essence, then your prayers, your good deeds, and your repentance do not 'cause' God to act differently—they are part of His eternal decree. How does that confront your view of why you should still pray and strive? Will you worship Him purely out of love and submission, not to manipulate His action?
?
The passage says that for created agents, the conditions for effectiveness are 'quickly changing.' Think of an area in your life where you feel powerless or lacking conditions. Does your desperation drive you to rely on the one whose action is never subject to changing circumstances? Will you entrust that area to God's unchanging will today?

Two Views of the Mutakallimun on the Preponderator
Objection presenting two mutakallimun views on the preponderator's role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two different positions held by the mutakallimun regarding whether the act of a capable agent requires a preponderator that leads to necessity or only to preference, and how they preserve the distinction between a capable agent and a necessitating cause.

Core Idea
The mutakallimun debated whether a preponderator makes an act necessary or merely preferred, preserving free choice.

This passage presents an objection that encapsulates a key debate within kalām: how can a capable agent (qādir) choose between two equally possible acts without a necessitating cause? The mutakallimun offered two main responses. The first holds that a preponderator makes the act more deserving (awlā) but not necessary; the second denies the need for any preponderator at all. Understanding these views is essential for grasping Islamic theological accounts of divine and human agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and two views
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice that this is an objection (fa-in qila) presenting two distinct statements from the mutakallimun.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the key terms
Locate the terms: preponderator (murjih), necessity (wujūb), more deserving (awlā), capable agent (qādir), and necessitating cause (illa mūjiba). Understand their roles in the two views.
These terms are technical and essential for kalām.
3
Reflect on the example
The second view gives an example of choosing between two identical cups. Think about how this illustrates the absence of a preponderator. Why does this example support the second view?
This example is meant to be intuitive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : للمتكلميين في هذا المقام : كلامان : الأول : قول من يقول : إن صدور الفعل عن القادر موقوف على المرجح، إلا أنه مع ذلك المرجح ، لا يصل إلى حد الوجوب ، بل يصير أولى بالوقوع ، فلأجل أنه صار أولى بالوقوع ، استغنى عن مرجح زائد . ولأجل أنه لا ينتهي إلى حد الوجوب ، بقي الفرق بين الموجب والقادر . والقول الثاني : إن صدور الفعل عن القادر لا يتوقف على انضمام المرجح إليه وتقريره : ما حكيناه عنهم : من أن المخير بين شرب قدحين ، وأكل رغيفين، يختار أحدهما على الآخر، لا المرجح . قالوا : والذي يدل على صحة ما ذكرناه : أن الفرق بين القادر المختار، وبين العلة الموجبة : معلوم .
For it is said: For the mutakallimun in this context are two statements: The first: The statement of one who says that the issuance of the act from the capable agent is dependent on the preponderator, but with that preponderator, it does not reach the level of necessity (wujub), rather it becomes more deserving (awla) of occurrence; so because it became more deserving of occurrence, it is independent of an additional preponderator, and because it does not reach the level of necessity, the difference between the necessitating cause (mujib) and the capable agent (qadir) remains. The second statement: that the issuance of the act from the capable agent is not dependent on the attachment of a preponderator to it. And its explanation is what we have related from them: that a person given the choice between drinking two cups and eating two loaves chooses one over the other without a preponderator. They said: And what indicates the correctness of what we have mentioned is that the difference between the capable choosing agent (al-qadir al-mukhtar) and the necessitating cause (al-illa al-mujiba) is known [by necessity].
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is an objection (fa-in qila) that presents two views of the mutakallimun regarding the role of the preponderator in the act of a capable agent. The first view holds that the act depends on a preponderator, but the preponderator only makes the act more deserving (awla) of occurrence, not necessary (wajib). Thus, the act is not necessitated, preserving the distinction between the capable agent (qadir) and the necessitating cause (mujib). The second view holds that the act does not depend on any preponderator at all, giving the example of a person who arbitrarily chooses between two similar options (e.g., drinking one of two cups) without any preponderating factor. They argue that the difference between a capable choosing agent and a necessitating cause is known intuitively.

Key Terms
متكلم
مرجح
وجوب
أولى
قادر مختار
علة موجبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all mutakallimun agree on necessity of a preponderator leading to necessity.
Correction: This passage shows two differing views: one where the preponderator leads only to preference (awlā), and another where no preponderator is needed at all.

Checkpoint
According to the first view mentioned in the objection, what is the status of the act after the preponderator?
A) The act becomes necessary.
B) The act becomes more deserving but not necessary.
C) The act is still equally possible.
D) The act is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun differed on whether a preponderator makes an act necessary or merely preferred, but both views maintain the distinction between a capable agent and a necessitating cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you find yourself acting more like a 'necessitating cause' (driven by compulsion) or a 'capable choosing agent'? What is one area where you can make a conscious choice that reflects your freedom as a responsible agent before Allah?
?
The mutakallimun debated whether a preponderator makes an act necessary or merely preferred. When you make a decision, do you sense a 'preponderator' pushing you, or do you feel a genuine freedom to choose otherwise? How does this awareness affect your sense of accountability for your actions?
?
If the difference between a capable agent and a necessitating cause is 'known by necessity' as the passage states, why do we sometimes live as if our actions are forced? What specific belief or habit in your life contradicts the intuitive knowledge that you are a qadir mukhtar?

Two States of the Agent: A Logical Puzzle
Author enumerates two states of an agent and their logical consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two states of an agent and why they seem to erase the difference between a voluntary agent and a necessitating cause.

Core Idea
Two states logically flatten all agents into one type — unless we look deeper.

The author begins by introducing a fundamental dichotomy for any cause: either all necessary conditions for its effect are eternally present, or they are not. This simple division seems to eliminate any meaningful distinction between a voluntary agent (al-qādir) and a necessitating cause (al-mūjib). Let's read and see why.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice the logical structure: two states are presented and then a conclusion.
The author uses a very concise style.
2
Identify the two states
Find the first state (all conditions present eternally) and the second state (conditions not present). Note the logical outcome for each: necessary action or impossible action.
The author uses 'يجب' and 'يمتنع' for necessity and impossibility.
3
Notice the apparent elimination of difference
The author says that on this basis, there remains no difference between qadir and mujib. Reflect on why this conclusion follows from the two-state model.
This sets up the need for a further distinction.
4
Prepare for the next lesson
Consider what additional factor might differentiate them. The commentary hints at the answer: changing conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
له حالتان : أحدهما : أن يكون كل ما لا بد منه في المؤثرية حاصلاً في الأزل والأخرى : أن لا يكون هذا المجموع حاصلا أما الحالة الأولى : فإنه يجب صدور الفعل عنه ، ويمتنع أن لا يصدر وأما الحالة الثانية : فإنه يمتنع صدور الفعل عنه ، ويجب عدمه . وعلى هذا التقدير فإنه لا يبقى فرق بين القادر وبين الموجب. بل الفرق : أن شرائط التأثير في حق القادر سريعة التغير ، فإذا حصلت بعد أن كانت معدومة ، صار القادر واجب التأثير . وإذا زالت بعد أن كانت موجودة ، صار ممتنع التأثير ، إلا أن هذا التغير إنما يعقل في حق من تكون مؤثريته موقوفة على شرائط منفصلة عن ذاته، أما الحق سبحانه فإن تأثيره فيما سواه غير موقوف على شرائط منفصلة عن ذاته ، لأنه تعالى مبدأ لكل ما سواه، فيمتنع أن يكون تأثيره فيما سواه موقوفاً على شرط منفصل، بل يجب أن يكون تأثيره في غيره لمحض ذاته ، ولوازم ذاته . ولما كانت ذاته ولوازم ذاته : ممتنعة التغير . كان تأثيره في غيره أيضاً : ممتنع التغير . فهذا هو الكلام القوي في هذا الباب
It has two states: one, that everything necessary for effective causation is present in eternity; the other, that this totality is not present. As for the first state: the action necessarily proceeds from it, and it is impossible that it does not proceed. As for the second state: it is impossible for the action to proceed from it, and its non-existence is necessary. On this basis, there remains no difference between the capable (al-qādir) and the necessitating cause (al-mūjib). Rather the difference is that the conditions of causation in the case of the capable (al-qādir) are quickly changing: if they become present after being absent, the capable becomes necessitating of effect; and if they cease after being present, it becomes impossible of effect. However, this change is only conceivable in the case of one whose causality depends on conditions separate from his essence. As for the Truth, Exalted is He, His effect on other-than-Him does not depend on conditions separate from His essence, because He, Exalted, is the principle of everything other than Him. So it is impossible that His effect on other-than-Him depends on a separate condition. Rather, His effect on other-than-Him must be solely by virtue of His essence and the necessities of His essence. And since His essence and the necessities of His essence are impossible of change, His effect on other-than-Him is also impossible of change. This is the strong speech on this topic.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage defines two states of an agent (or cause) with respect to its effect, then distinguishes between a voluntary agent (al-qādir) and a necessitating cause (al-mūjib), and finally applies the distinction to God. The author states that any cause has two states: either all necessary conditions for causation obtain eternally, or they do not. In the first state, the effect is necessary; in the second, it is impossible. This would seem to erase the difference between a voluntary agent and a necessitating cause. However, the author explains the difference lies in the speed of change of conditions: in created voluntary agents, conditions change rapidly, so the agent becomes necessary at the moment conditions are complete and impossible when they are absent. But this change only makes sense for beings whose causality depends on conditions separate from their essence. God, being the First Principle, cannot depend on external conditions; His effect is by His essence alone and its necessities. Since His essence is immutable, His effect is also immutable and necessary. This is presented as the definitive argument on the subject.

قادر
موجب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if all necessary conditions for causation are present eternally, what is the logical status of the action?
A) necessary
B) possible
C) impossible
D) contingent

Key Takeaway
The two states of an agent (conditions eternally present or not) lead to a necessary or impossible effect, which seemingly eliminates any difference between a voluntary agent and a necessitating cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your every action were determined by pre-existing conditions, would you still consider yourself free? How does this lesson's logical puzzle challenge your personal sense of responsibility?
?
When you think about your ability to choose, do you see yourself as a قادر (truly capable) or merely driven by circumstance? What would it take for you to act as a real agent?
?
This passage shows that without a deeper analysis, even God's actions would appear necessary like a natural cause. How does that realization affect the way you think about your own actions—are they your own or forced? What will you do today to act as a truly voluntary agent?

Causality and Created Things

The Real Difference: Changing Conditions and Divine Immutability
Author introduces the real difference and applies it to divine causation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the real difference between a voluntary agent and a necessitating cause lies in the changeability of conditions, and why this distinction applies only to created beings, not to God.

Core Idea
The difference is change, and God has no external conditions to change.

After showing that the simple two-state model fails to distinguish, the author now provides the real criterion: the speed of change in the conditions of causation. This allows him to separate created voluntary agents from necessitating causes, and ultimately to argue that God's causation is immutable.

Guided Path
1
Read the second half of the passage
Read from 'بل الفرق' to the end. Note the introduction of the real difference: the conditions of causation are quickly changing in the case of the capable (qādir).
2
Understand the distinction for created beings
The author explains that for a voluntary agent (like a human), when conditions are complete, the agent becomes necessitating of effect; when they cease, the effect becomes impossible. This is the difference: the conditions change.
This shows that qādir is not always qādir; it becomes mūjib when conditions are met.
3
Apply to God
The author points out that this change only applies to beings whose causality depends on separate conditions. God's effect depends only on His essence and its necessities, which are immutable. Hence, God's causation is also immutable.
This is the 'strong speech' on the topic.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider how this argument preserves both divine transcendence (no change) and the uniqueness of God's causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
له حالتان : أحدهما : أن يكون كل ما لا بد منه في المؤثرية حاصلاً في الأزل والأخرى : أن لا يكون هذا المجموع حاصلا أما الحالة الأولى : فإنه يجب صدور الفعل عنه ، ويمتنع أن لا يصدر وأما الحالة الثانية : فإنه يمتنع صدور الفعل عنه ، ويجب عدمه . وعلى هذا التقدير فإنه لا يبقى فرق بين القادر وبين الموجب. بل الفرق : أن شرائط التأثير في حق القادر سريعة التغير ، فإذا حصلت بعد أن كانت معدومة ، صار القادر واجب التأثير . وإذا زالت بعد أن كانت موجودة ، صار ممتنع التأثير ، إلا أن هذا التغير إنما يعقل في حق من تكون مؤثريته موقوفة على شرائط منفصلة عن ذاته، أما الحق سبحانه فإن تأثيره فيما سواه غير موقوف على شرائط منفصلة عن ذاته ، لأنه تعالى مبدأ لكل ما سواه، فيمتنع أن يكون تأثيره فيما سواه موقوفاً على شرط منفصل، بل يجب أن يكون تأثيره في غيره لمحض ذاته ، ولوازم ذاته . ولما كانت ذاته ولوازم ذاته : ممتنعة التغير . كان تأثيره في غيره أيضاً : ممتنع التغير . فهذا هو الكلام القوي في هذا الباب
It has two states: one, that everything necessary for effective causation is present in eternity; the other, that this totality is not present. As for the second state: it is impossible for the action to proceed from it, and its non-existence is necessary. So it is impossible that His effect on other-than-Him depends on a separate condition. Rather, His effect on other-than-Him must be solely by virtue of His essence and the necessities of His essence. And since His essence and the necessities of His essence are impossible of change, His effect on other-than-Him is also impossible of change. This is the strong speech on this topic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's action is arbitrary or can change over time.
Correction: The passage argues that God's effect is necessary and immutable because it flows from His immutable essence, not from external conditions.

Checkpoint
What is the reason why God's effect cannot change, according to the passage?
A) God has perfect knowledge
B) God's will is eternal
C) God's effect is by His essence and its necessities, which are unchanging
D) God's power is infinite

Key Takeaway
The real distinction between a voluntary agent and a necessitating cause is the changeability of conditions; since God has no external conditions, His causation is necessary and immutable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often attribute your successes or failures to changing circumstances. This lesson teaches that God's action is not subject to change. How does your reliance on conditions (health, wealth, status) for your spiritual state reveal a hidden belief that God's agency works like yours? What would it look like to trust in God's unchanging essence rather than your shifting conditions?
?
The author says God's effect is solely by His essence and its necessities. If you truly believed that God's causation requires nothing outside Him, how would it change the way you pray? Do your supplications ask God to change external conditions, or do they seek alignment with His immutable will? Examine your most recent dua—what does it reveal about your understanding of God's causation?
?
Think of a disappointment where you felt God did not act as you expected. Does this lesson challenge your assumption that God's action should follow the pattern of human agency (i.e., responding to changing conditions)? How can you reconcile your expectation with the truth that God's effect is immutable and necessary from His essence? What would it mean for you to accept His decrees as arising from His perfect essence, not from changing circumstances?
